Low prevalence dramatically reduces PPV.

- **[R] D4** — If P(A) = 0.5, P(B) = 0.4, and P(A and B) = 0.2, are events A and B independent?
  - A) Yes, because P(A and B) = P(A) × P(B) = 0.5 × 0.4 = 0.2.  B) No, because P(A and B) should equal P(A) + P(B) for independent events.  C) Yes, because A and B are not mutually exclusive.  D) No, because the events overlap.
  - Answer: **A** — Two events are independent if P(A ∩ B) = P(A) × P(B). Here: P(A) × P(B) = 0.5 × 0.4 = 0.20, which equals P(A and B) = 0.20. Therefore A and B are independent. Note: independence and mutual exclusivity are different concepts — mutually exclusive events (except trivial cases) are NOT independent.

- **[R] D5** — The standard deviation of a binomial random variable with n = 100 and p = 0.3 is:
  - A) √21 ≈ 4.58  B) √30 ≈ 5.48  C) √(100 × 0.3) = 5.48  D) √(0.3 × 0.7) ≈ 0.46
  - Answer: **A** — SD of a binomial = √(np(1−p)) = √(100 × 0.3 × 0.7) = √21 ≈ 4.58. Note: np = 30 is the mean, not the standard deviation. √30 is a common distractor from confusing mean and variance.

- **[U] D2** — A bag contains 5 red and 3 blue marbles. If two marbles are drawn without replacement, what is the probability that both are red?
  - A) 5/16  B) 5/14  C) 25/64  D) 10/56
  - Answer: **B** — P(both red) = P(1st red) × P(2nd red | 1st red) = (5/8) × (4/7) = 20/56 = 5/14. After drawing one red marble, 4 red and 3 blue remain (7 total).

- **[U] D3** — The probability that a student passes math is 0.7. The probability that a student passes both math and science is 0.5. Given that a student passes math, what is the probability they also pass science?
  - A) 0.35  B) 0.50  C) 0.71  D) 0.75
  - Answer: **C** — P(Science | Math) = P(Math ∩ Science) / P(Math) = 0.5 / 0.7 ≈ 0.714 ≈ 0.71. This is the conditional probability formula: P(B|A) = P(A ∩ B) / P(A).

- **[U] D3** — A binomial setting requires four conditions (BINS). Which of the following is NOT one of those conditions?
  - A) Binary outcomes (success or failure)  B) Independent trials  C) Normal distribution of outcomes  D) Fixed number of trials (n)
  - Answer: **C** — The four BINS conditions for a binomial setting are: Binary outcomes, Independent trials, fixed Number of trials (n), and same probability of Success (p) for each trial. A normal distribution of outcomes is NOT required for a binomial setting (though the sampling distribution of the count approximates normal for large n).


#### Sampling Dist

- **[A] D3** — A sampling distribution of p̂ (sample proportion) is approximately normal when:
  - A) n > 30  B) np ≥ 10 and n(1 − p) ≥ 10  C) p > 0.5  D) The population size exceeds 1000
  - Answer: **B** — The sampling distribution of p̂ is approximately normal when both np ≥ 10 and n(1−p) ≥ 10 (the Large Counts condition). This ensures there are enough expected successes and failures. The condition n > 30 applies to sample means, not proportions.

- **[A] D3** — The mean of the sampling distribution of p̂ is:
  - A) p/n  B) p̂  C) p  D) √(p(1−p)/n)
  - Answer: **C** — The sampling distribution of p̂ is centered at the true population proportion p. That is, E(p̂) = p, making p̂ an unbiased estimator of p. The standard deviation of the sampling distribution is √(p(1−p)/n), not the mean.

- **[F] D1** — The Central Limit Theorem (CLT) states that for large sample sizes, the sampling distribution of the sample mean is:
  - A) Identical to the population distribution.  B) Approximately normal, regardless of the shape of the population distribution.  C) Skewed in the same direction as the population.  D) Always exactly normal for any sample size.
  - Answer: **B** — The CLT states that for sufficiently large n (generally n ≥ 30 as a rule of thumb), the sampling distribution of x̄ is approximately normal, regardless of the population's shape. This is one of the most powerful results in statistics.

- **[F] D2** — A population has mean μ = 50 and standard deviation σ = 10. What is the standard error of the sample mean for samples of size n = 25?
  - A) 0.4  B) 2  C) 10  D) 50
  - Answer: **B** — Standard error (SE) of the sample mean = σ/√n = 10/√25 = 10/5 = 2. The standard error measures the typical distance between the sample mean and the population mean across repeated samples.

- **[R] D4** — A student says: 'The Central Limit Theorem says the sample data will be normal if n is large.' What is wrong with this statement?
  - A) Nothing — the CLT applies to individual data values for large n.  B) The CLT applies to the sampling distribution of the sample mean, not to individual data values in the sample.  C) The CLT only applies when the population is already normal.  D) The CLT requires n ≥ 100, not just 'large n.'
  - Answer: **B** — This is a critical distinction. The CLT guarantees that the sampling distribution of the sample mean (x̄) becomes approximately normal for large n, not that the individual data values become normal. The sample data retains the shape of the population distribution regardless of sample size.

- **[R] D5** — Two researchers each take samples from the same population (μ = 100, σ = 20). Researcher A uses n = 25; Researcher B uses n = 100. Which statement about their sampling distributions is correct?
  - A) Both have the same standard error of 20.  B) Researcher A's sampling distribution has SE = 4; Researcher B's has SE = 2.  C) Researcher B's sampling distribution has a higher mean because of the larger sample.  D) Researcher A's estimates will be more precise because smaller samples have less bias.
  - Answer: **B** — SE_A = 20/√25 = 4; SE_B = 20/√100 = 2. Both sampling distributions are centered at μ = 100 (unbiased). Researcher B's estimates are more precise (lower SE). Sample size affects precision, not bias (both estimators are unbiased). Larger samples produce narrower sampling distributions.

- **[U] D2** — As sample size increases, the standard error of the sample mean:
  - A) Increases proportionally to n.  B) Remains constant regardless of n.  C) Decreases — larger samples produce more precise estimates.  D) Increases then decreases at n = 30.
  - Answer: **C** — SE = σ/√n. As n increases, √n increases, so SE decreases. Larger samples reduce sampling variability and produce more precise estimates of the population mean. This is why larger samples are better.

- **[U] D3** — A population has mean 80 and standard deviation 16. Samples of size n = 64 are taken. What is the probability that a sample mean exceeds 82?
  - A) Approximately 0.16  B) Approximately 0.84  C) Approximately 0.025  D) Approximately 0.975
  - Answer: **A** — SE = 16/√64 = 2. z = (82 − 80)/2 = 1.0. P(x̄ > 82) = P(z > 1) ≈ 1 − 0.8413 = 0.1587 ≈ 0.16. Using the standard normal table, about 16% of samples of size 64 will have a mean above 82.


#### Two Var Data

- **[A] D3** — A study finds a correlation of r = 0.95 between ice cream sales and drowning rates. A reporter concludes that eating ice cream causes drowning. What is the most appropriate statistical response?
  - A) The reporter is correct because r > 0.9 confirms causation.  B) Correlation does not imply causation; hot weather is likely a lurking variable that increases both ice cream sales and swimming (and thus drowning).  C) The correlation should be recalculated after removing outliers to confirm the causal link.  D) Since r is positive, ice cream protects against drowning.
  - Answer: **B** — This is a classic example of confounding/lurking variables. High temperature (summer) causes both increased ice cream sales and increased swimming activity (which raises drowning risk). Correlation measures association, not causation. A lurking variable (temperature) drives both variables simultaneously.

- **[F] D1** — A correlation coefficient of r = −0.92 between hours of TV watched and GPA indicates:
  - A) Watching TV causes lower GPA.  B) There is a strong negative linear relationship between hours of TV watched and GPA.  C) There is a weak negative relationship between the two variables.  D) GPA decreases by 0.92 for each additional hour of TV watched.
  - Answer: **B** — r = −0.92 is close to −1, indicating a strong negative linear association. Correlation does not imply causation, so we cannot say TV watching causes lower GPA. The value of r is not a slope — it measures the strength and direction of the linear relationship.

- **[F] D2** — The least-squares regression line (LSRL) for predicting weight (lbs) from height (in) is: ŷ = −100 + 5x. What is the predicted weight for a person who is 65 inches tall?
  - A) 225 lbs  B) 235 lbs  C) 250 lbs  D) 325 lbs
  - Answer: **A** — ŷ = −100 + 5(65) = −100 + 325 = 225 lbs. Substitute x = 65 into the regression equation.

- **[R] D4** — The LSRL for predicting salary (in thousands) from years of experience is ŷ = 40 + 3.2x. A person with 10 years of experience earns $78,000. What is the residual?
  - A) −$6,000  B) +$6,000  C) +$4,000  D) +$38,000
  - Answer: **B** — Predicted: ŷ = 40 + 3.2(10) = 40 + 32 = 72 (thousands) = $72,000. Residual = Actual − Predicted = 78 − 72 = +6 (thousands) = +$6,000. A positive residual means the actual salary exceeded the model's prediction.

- **[U] D2** — In a regression analysis, r² = 0.81. Which statement correctly interprets this value?
  - A) The correlation between the variables is 0.81.  B) 81% of the variation in the response variable is explained by the linear relationship with the explanatory variable.  C) The regression line predicts the response variable with 81% accuracy.  D) There is a 0.81 probability that the regression line is correct.
  - Answer: **B** — r² (the coefficient of determination) represents the proportion of variability in the response variable that is explained by the linear regression model. r² = 0.81 means 81% of the variation in y is accounted for by the linear relationship with x. Note: r = ±0.9, not 0.81.

- **[U] D3** — A residual plot for a linear regression shows a curved (U-shaped) pattern. What does this indicate?
  - A) The linear model is a good fit for the data.  B) The data has high variability that cannot be modeled.  C) A linear model is not appropriate; a nonlinear model may be a better fit.  D) The residuals are normally distributed, confirming the model is valid.
  - Answer: **C** — A residual plot should show random scatter around zero if the linear model is appropriate. A U-shaped or curved pattern indicates a systematic trend that the linear model is not capturing, suggesting that a nonlinear (e.g., quadratic) model may be more appropriate.

---

### Geometry (75 questions)


#### Area Volume

- **[A] D3** — A rectangular swimming pool is 20 m long, 10 m wide, and 2 m deep. How many cubic meters of water does it hold?
  - A) 200 m³  B) 320 m³  C) 400 m³  D) 600 m³
  - Answer: **C** — Volume = 20 × 10 × 2 = 400 m³.

- **[A] D3** — A cone has radius 4 cm and height 9 cm. What is its volume? (Use π)
  - A) 12π cm³  B) 36π cm³  C) 48π cm³  D) 144π cm³
  - Answer: **C** — Volume of cone = (1/3)πr²h = (1/3)π(16)(9) = 48π cm³.

- **[A] D4** — A sphere has radius 6 cm. What is its volume? (Use π; V = (4/3)πr³)
  - A) 144π cm³  B) 216π cm³  C) 288π cm³  D) 864π cm³
  - Answer: **C** — V = (4/3)π(6)³ = (4/3)π(216) = 288π cm³.

- **[A] D4** — A triangular prism has a triangular base with base 6 and height 4, and a prism height of 10. What is its volume?
  - A) 60  B) 120  C) 240  D) 480
  - Answer: **B** — Area of triangular base = (1/2)(6)(4) = 12. Volume = base area × prism height = 12 × 10 = 120.

- **[F] D1** — What is the area of a triangle with base 10 cm and height 8 cm?
  - A) 40 cm²  B) 80 cm²  C) 18 cm²  D) 20 cm²
  - Answer: **A** — Area of triangle = (1/2) × base × height = (1/2) × 10 × 8 = 40 cm².

- **[F] D1** — What is the volume of a rectangular prism with length 5, width 4, and height 3?
  - A) 12  B) 47  C) 60  D) 120
  - Answer: **C** — Volume = length × width × height = 5 × 4 × 3 = 60.

- **[F] D2** — A cylinder has radius 3 cm and height 10 cm. What is its volume? (Use π)
  - A) 30π cm³  B) 60π cm³  C) 90π cm³  D) 900π cm³
  - Answer: **C** — Volume of cylinder = πr²h = π(9)(10) = 90π cm³.

- **[R] D4** — A cylinder and a cone have the same radius and height. What is the ratio of the cylinder's volume to the cone's volume?
  - A) 1:3  B) 2:1  C) 3:1  D) 1:2
  - Answer: **C** — V_cylinder = πr²h; V_cone = (1/3)πr²h. Ratio = πr²h / (1/3)πr²h = 3:1.

- **[R] D5** — A cone is inscribed in a cylinder of radius 5 and height 12. What fraction of the cylinder's volume is occupied by the cone?
  - A) 1/4  B) 1/3  C) 1/2  D) 2/3
  - Answer: **B** — V_cone = (1/3)πr²h. V_cylinder = πr²h. Fraction = (1/3)πr²h / πr²h = 1/3.

- **[U] D2** — A parallelogram has base 12 ft and height 7 ft. What is its area?
  - A) 38 ft²  B) 42 ft²  C) 84 ft²  D) 19 ft²
  - Answer: **C** — Area of parallelogram = base × height = 12 × 7 = 84 ft².

- **[U] D2** — A trapezoid has parallel bases of 6 and 10, and a height of 4. What is its area?
  - A) 32  B) 40  C) 64  D) 60
  - Answer: **A** — Area of trapezoid = (1/2)(b₁ + b₂)(h) = (1/2)(6 + 10)(4) = (1/2)(16)(4) = 32.

- **[U] D3** — What is the surface area of a cube with side length 5?
  - A) 25  B) 75  C) 125  D) 150
  - Answer: **D** — A cube has 6 faces. Surface area = 6 × s² = 6 × 25 = 150.


#### Circles

- **[A] D3** — A chord is 16 cm long. It is 6 cm from the center of the circle. What is the radius?
  - A) 8 cm  B) 10 cm  C) 12 cm  D) 14 cm
  - Answer: **B** — The perpendicular from center to chord bisects it: half-chord = 8 cm. r² = 8² + 6² = 64 + 36 = 100. r = 10 cm.

- **[A] D3** — A circle has diameter 14. What is the length of an arc intercepted by a central angle of 60°?
  - A) 7π/3  B) 7π  C) 14π/6  D) 14π/3
  - Answer: **A** — Radius = 7. Arc length = (60/360) × 2πr = (1/6) × 14π = 7π/3.

- **[A] D4** — Identify the center and radius of the circle (x + 5)² + (y − 1)² = 49.
  - A) Center (5, −1), r = 7  B) Center (−5, 1), r = 49  C) Center (−5, 1), r = 7  D) Center (5, 1), r = 7
  - Answer: **C** — Standard form (x − h)² + (y − k)² = r². Here h = −5, k = 1, r² = 49 → r = 7. Center (−5, 1), radius 7.

- **[F] D1** — A circle has radius 9. What is its circumference? (Use π)
  - A) 9π  B) 18π  C) 81π  D) 27π
  - Answer: **B** — Circumference = 2πr = 2π(9) = 18π.

- **[F] D1** — A central angle of a circle intercepts an arc of 80°. What is the measure of the central angle?
  - A) 40°  B) 80°  C) 160°  D) 320°
  - Answer: **B** — A central angle equals the intercepted arc. Central angle = 80°.

- **[F] D2** — A circle has radius 6. What is the area of a sector with a central angle of 90°?
  - A) 9π  B) 12π  C) 18π  D) 36π
  - Answer: **A** — Sector area = (central angle/360°) × πr² = (90/360) × π(36) = (1/4) × 36π = 9π.

- **[R] D4** — Two secants from the same external point intercept arcs of 80° and 30°. What is the angle at the external point?
  - A) 25°  B) 35°  C) 40°  D) 55°
  - Answer: **A** — Angle = (1/2)|arc₁ − arc₂| = (1/2)|80° − 30°| = (1/2)(50°) = 25°.

- **[R] D4** — Two chords intersect inside a circle. One chord is divided into segments of 3 and 8. The other chord's shorter segment is 4. What is the longer segment?
  - A) 5  B) 6  C) 7  D) 8
  - Answer: **B** — Intersecting Chords Theorem: product of segments are equal. 3 × 8 = 4 × x → 24 = 4x → x = 6.

- **[R] D5** — A tangent and a secant are drawn from an external point. The tangent has length 12 and the secant's external segment is 6. What is the secant's total length?
  - A) 18  B) 24  C) 30  D) 36
  - Answer: **C** — Tangent-Secant theorem: tangent² = external segment × whole secant. 144 = 6 × whole → whole = 24. Wait: 12² = 6 × whole → 144 = 6 × whole → whole = 24. Answer B.

- **[U] D2** — An inscribed angle intercepts an arc of 100°. What is the measure of the inscribed angle?
  - A) 50°  B) 100°  C) 200°  D) 25°
  - Answer: **A** — An inscribed angle equals half the intercepted arc: 100°/2 = 50°.

- **[U] D2** — What is the equation of a circle with center (3, −2) and radius 5?
  - A) (x − 3)² + (y + 2)² = 5  B) (x + 3)² + (y − 2)² = 25  C) (x − 3)² + (y + 2)² = 25  D) (x − 3)² + (y − 2)² = 25
  - Answer: **C** — Standard form: (x − h)² + (y − k)² = r². Center (3, −2): (x−3)² + (y+2)² = 25.

- **[U] D3** — A tangent line from an external point touches the circle at exactly one point. What is the angle between the tangent and the radius at the point of tangency?
  - A) 45°  B) 60°  C) 90°  D) 180°
  - Answer: **C** — A tangent line is perpendicular to the radius drawn to the point of tangency. The angle is always 90°.


#### Congruence Triangles

- **[A] D3** — Triangle ABC ≅ Triangle DEF. If AB = 12, BC = 15, AC = 18, what is EF?
  - A) 12  B) 15  C) 18  D) Cannot be determined
  - Answer: **B** — By CPCTC, corresponding parts of congruent triangles are congruent. BC corresponds to EF, so EF = 15.

- **[A] D3** — Two right triangles have equal hypotenuses and one pair of equal legs. Which postulate proves them congruent?
  - A) SAS  B) ASA  C) HL  D) AAS
  - Answer: **C** — HL (Hypotenuse-Leg) applies only to right triangles: if the hypotenuse and one leg are congruent, the triangles are congruent.

- **[A] D4** — An exterior angle of a triangle measures 110°. One non-adjacent interior angle measures 65°. What is the other non-adjacent interior angle?
  - A) 35°  B) 45°  C) 55°  D) 70°
  - Answer: **B** — Exterior Angle Theorem: exterior angle = sum of the two non-adjacent interior angles. 110° = 65° + x → x = 45°.

- **[F] D1** — Two triangles have all three pairs of corresponding sides equal. Which congruence postulate applies?
  - A) SAS  B) ASA  C) SSS  D) AAS
  - Answer: **C** — SSS (Side-Side-Side) postulate: if all three sides of one triangle equal the corresponding sides of another, the triangles are congruent.

- **[F] D1** — In triangle ABC, AB = AC. What type of triangle is ABC?
  - A) Equilateral  B) Scalene  C) Isosceles  D) Right
  - Answer: **C** — A triangle with at least two equal sides is isosceles. AB = AC means two sides are equal.

- **[F] D2** — The base angles of an isosceles triangle measure 52° each. What is the measure of the vertex angle?
  - A) 52°  B) 76°  C) 128°  D) 90°
  - Answer: **B** — Sum of angles = 180°. Vertex = 180° − 52° − 52° = 76°.

- **[R] D4** — Triangle PQR has PQ = PR. If angle Q = (3x + 10)° and angle R = (5x − 8)°, find x.
  - A) 6  B) 9  C) 12  D) 18
  - Answer: **B** — Base angles of isosceles triangle are equal: 3x + 10 = 5x − 8 → 18 = 2x → x = 9.

- **[R] D4** — Which additional information is sufficient to prove △ABC ≅ △XYZ by ASA, given ∠A = ∠X and AC = XZ?
  - A) BC = YZ  B) AB = XY  C) ∠C = ∠Z  D) ∠B = ∠Y
  - Answer: **C** — ASA needs two angles and the included side. We have ∠A = ∠X and side AC = XZ. The included angle at C must equal ∠Z to complete ASA.

- **[R] D5** — In △ABC, a median is drawn from vertex A to midpoint M of BC. Which statement is always true?
  - A) AM bisects ∠A  B) AM ⊥ BC  C) BM = MC  D) △ABM ≅ △ACM
  - Answer: **C** — A median connects a vertex to the midpoint of the opposite side. By definition, BM = MC. The median does not necessarily bisect the angle or be perpendicular to BC.

- **[R] D5** — Two triangles are congruent. One has angles 40°, 60°, 80°. The other has sides in ratio 3:4:5. Which statement is true?
  - A) They must be right triangles  B) They cannot be congruent if they have different side ratios  C) Congruence requires both equal angles AND equal side lengths  D) They are congruent because the angles match
  - Answer: **C** — Congruence requires equal angles AND equal side lengths (same size and shape). Equal angles only proves similarity. The 3:4:5 triangle with 40-60-80° angles could have any size.

- **[U] D2** — Two triangles share a side. Two angles of one triangle equal two angles of the other. Which postulate proves them congruent?
  - A) SSS  B) SAS  C) ASA  D) AAS
  - Answer: **D** — AAS (Angle-Angle-Side): two angles and a non-included side are congruent. The shared side is the non-included side.

- **[U] D2** — Which postulate requires two sides and the INCLUDED angle to be congruent?
  - A) SSS  B) SAS  C) AAS  D) HL
  - Answer: **B** — SAS (Side-Angle-Side): two sides and the angle between them must be congruent.

- **[U] D3** — In an equilateral triangle, each interior angle measures:
  - A) 45°  B) 60°  C) 90°  D) 120°
  - Answer: **B** — An equilateral triangle has three equal angles. 180° ÷ 3 = 60° each.

- **[U] D4** — Which set of side lengths CANNOT form a triangle?
  - A) 3, 4, 5  B) 5, 7, 10  C) 6, 6, 11  D) 2, 4, 7
  - Answer: **D** — Triangle Inequality: the sum of any two sides must exceed the third. 2 + 4 = 6 < 7, so 2, 4, 7 cannot form a triangle.


#### Right Triangles Trig

- **[A] D3** — A ladder 20 feet long leans against a wall. The base is 8 feet from the wall. How high does the ladder reach?
  - A) √336 ≈ 18.3 ft  B) 12 ft  C) 16 ft  D) √464 ≈ 21.5 ft
  - Answer: **A** — h² = 20² − 8² = 400 − 64 = 336. h = √336 ≈ 18.3 feet.

- **[A] D3** — A 30-60-90 triangle has a hypotenuse of 18. What is the length of the longer leg?
  - A) 9  B) 9√3  C) 18√3  D) 6√3
  - Answer: **B** — Shorter leg = hypotenuse/2 = 9. Longer leg = shorter leg × √3 = 9√3.

- **[A] D3** — From the top of a 50-foot cliff, the angle of depression to a boat is 30°. How far is the boat from the base of the cliff?
  - A) 25 ft  B) 50√3 ft  C) 50/√3 ft  D) 25√3 ft
  - Answer: **B** — tan(30°) = opposite/adjacent = 50/d. d = 50/tan(30°) = 50/(1/√3) = 50√3 ≈ 86.6 ft.

- **[A] D4** — A ramp rises 4 feet over a horizontal distance of 20 feet. What is the angle of elevation to the nearest degree? (tan⁻¹(0.2) ≈ 11.3°)
  - A) about 11°  B) about 15°  C) about 20°  D) about 78°
  - Answer: **A** — tan(θ) = opposite/adjacent = 4/20 = 0.2. θ = tan⁻¹(0.2) ≈ 11.3° ≈ 11°.

- **[F] D1** — A right triangle has legs 6 and 8. What is the hypotenuse?
  - A) 10  B) 12  C) 14  D) √100
  - Answer: **A** — Pythagorean Theorem: c² = 6² + 8² = 36 + 64 = 100. c = 10.

- **[F] D1** — In a 45-45-90 triangle, if the legs are each 7, what is the hypotenuse?
  - A) 7√2  B) 7√3  C) 14  D) 7/√2
  - Answer: **A** — In a 45-45-90 triangle, hypotenuse = leg × √2 = 7√2.

- **[F] D2** — In a right triangle, if one leg is 5 and the hypotenuse is 13, what is the other leg?
  - A) 8  B) 12  C) √144  D) 10
  - Answer: **B** — b² = 13² − 5² = 169 − 25 = 144. b = 12.

- **[R] D4** — In right triangle ABC, sin(A) = 3/5. What is cos(A)?
  - A) 3/4  B) 4/5  C) 5/3  D) 4/3
  - Answer: **B** — If sin(A) = 3/5, then opposite = 3, hypotenuse = 5. Adjacent = √(25−9) = 4. cos(A) = 4/5.

- **[R] D4** — Which trigonometric ratio is equal to sin(60°)?
  - A) sin(30°)  B) cos(30°)  C) cos(60°)  D) tan(45°)
  - Answer: **B** — Complementary angles: sin(θ) = cos(90° − θ). sin(60°) = cos(30°) = √3/2.

- **[R] D5** — In △ABC, angle B = 90°, AB = 7, BC = 24. What is tan(A)?
  - A) 7/25  B) 24/25  C) 24/7  D) 7/24
  - Answer: **C** — tan(A) = opposite/adjacent. Opposite to A is BC = 24. Adjacent to A is AB = 7. tan(A) = 24/7.

- **[R] D5** — A surveyor stands 100 m from the base of a building. The angle of elevation to the top is 58°. Which expression gives the building's height? (sin 58° ≈ 0.848, cos 58° ≈ 0.530, tan 58° ≈ 1.600)
  - A) 100 × sin(58°)  B) 100 / tan(58°)  C) 100 × tan(58°)  D) 100 × cos(58°)
  - Answer: **C** — tan(58°) = height/100 → height = 100 × tan(58°) ≈ 100 × 1.600 = 160 m.

- **[U] D2** — In a 30-60-90 triangle, the shorter leg is 5. What is the hypotenuse?
  - A) 5√3  B) 10  C) 5√2  D) 10√3
  - Answer: **B** — In a 30-60-90 triangle, hypotenuse = 2 × shorter leg = 2 × 5 = 10.

- **[U] D2** — In right triangle ABC with right angle C, which ratio equals sin(A)?
  - A) adjacent/hypotenuse  B) hypotenuse/opposite  C) opposite/hypotenuse  D) adjacent/opposite
  - Answer: **C** — SOH: Sin = Opposite/Hypotenuse. sin(A) = side opposite to A / hypotenuse.

- **[U] D3** — In right triangle XYZ with right angle at Z, XZ = 3 and XY = 5. What is cos(X)?
  - A) 3/5  B) 4/5  C) 3/4  D) 5/3
  - Answer: **A** — cos(X) = adjacent/hypotenuse. Adjacent to X is XZ = 3. Hypotenuse = XY = 5. cos(X) = 3/5.


#### Similarity

- **[A] D3** — A dilation with center at the origin and scale factor 3 maps point A(2, 4) to A'. What are the coordinates of A'?
  - A) (5, 7)  B) (6, 4)  C) (6, 12)  D) (2/3, 4/3)
  - Answer: **C** — Dilation multiplies each coordinate by the scale factor: A' = (2×3, 4×3) = (6, 12).

- **[A] D3** — In △ABC, DE is parallel to BC with D on AB and E on AC. If AD = 4, DB = 6, and BC = 15, find DE.
  - A) 6  B) 9  C) 10  D) 12
  - Answer: **A** — By the Triangle Proportionality Theorem: DE/BC = AD/AB = 4/(4+6) = 4/10 = 2/5. DE = 15 × 2/5 = 6.

- **[A] D4** — A photo is 4 inches wide and 6 inches tall. It is enlarged so the width becomes 10 inches. What is the new height?
  - A) 12 in  B) 15 in  C) 16 in  D) 24 in
  - Answer: **B** — Scale factor = 10/4 = 2.5. New height = 6 × 2.5 = 15 inches.

- **[F] D1** — Two triangles are similar. One has sides 3, 4, 5. The other has shortest side 9. What is its longest side?
  - A) 12  B) 15  C) 20  D) 25
  - Answer: **B** — Scale factor = 9/3 = 3. Longest side = 5 × 3 = 15.

- **[F] D2** — Which postulate proves two triangles similar if two pairs of corresponding angles are congruent?
  - A) SSS similarity  B) SAS similarity  C) AA similarity  D) HL similarity
  - Answer: **C** — AA (Angle-Angle) similarity: if two angles of one triangle equal two angles of another, the triangles are similar.

- **[R] D3** — For SAS similarity, which must be true?
  - A) Two sides and any angle are proportional  B) Two sides are proportional and the included angle is congruent  C) All three sides are proportional  D) Two angles are congruent
  - Answer: **B** — SAS similarity: two pairs of corresponding sides are proportional AND the included angle is congruent.

- **[R] D4** — A dilation maps △ABC to △A'B'C' with scale factor k = 1/2. Which is true?
  - A) △A'B'C' is larger than △ABC  B) △A'B'C' is congruent to △ABC  C) △A'B'C' is smaller than △ABC and similar to △ABC  D) △A'B'C' has different angle measures than △ABC
  - Answer: **C** — A scale factor of 1/2 creates a smaller image (reduction). Dilations preserve shape (angles) but change size, so the triangles are similar but not congruent.

- **[R] D5** — In a right triangle, the altitude drawn to the hypotenuse creates two smaller triangles. Which is always true?
  - A) The two smaller triangles are congruent to each other  B) Each smaller triangle is similar to the original triangle  C) The altitude equals half the hypotenuse  D) The two smaller triangles are congruent to the original
  - Answer: **B** — Geometric Mean (Altitude) Theorem: the altitude to the hypotenuse of a right triangle creates two triangles each similar to the original and to each other.

- **[U] D2** — A flagpole casts a 12-foot shadow at the same time a 6-foot person casts a 4-foot shadow. How tall is the flagpole?
  - A) 8 ft  B) 16 ft  C) 18 ft  D) 24 ft
  - Answer: **C** — Using similar triangles (same angle of sun): h/12 = 6/4 → h = 6 × 12/4 = 18 feet.

- **[U] D2** — Triangle ABC ~ Triangle DEF with ratio 2:5. If DE = 10, what is AB?
  - A) 2  B) 4  C) 5  D) 25
  - Answer: **B** — AB/DE = 2/5 → AB = DE × 2/5 = 10 × 2/5 = 4.

- **[U] D3** — If two triangles are similar with ratio 3:7, what is the ratio of their areas?
  - A) 3:7  B) 6:14  C) 9:49  D) 27:343
  - Answer: **C** — The ratio of areas of similar figures is the square of the similarity ratio: (3/7)² = 9/49.

- **[U] D5** — Two similar solids have surface areas of 25 cm² and 100 cm². What is the ratio of their volumes?
  - A) 1:4  B) 1:8  C) 1:16  D) 5:10
  - Answer: **B** — Surface area ratio = (similarity ratio)². 25:100 = 1:4, so similarity ratio = 1:2. Volume ratio = (1:2)³ = 1:8.


#### Transformations

- **[A] D3** — Triangle PQR has vertices P(1,2), Q(3,2), R(2,4). After a reflection over the line y = x, what is the image of P?
  - A) (2, 1)  B) (−1, 2)  C) (1, −2)  D) (2, −1)
  - Answer: **A** — Reflection over y = x: (x, y) → (y, x). P(1,2) → P'(2, 1).

- **[A] D3** — A figure is dilated by a scale factor of 3 from the origin. A point on the figure is (2, 4). Where does it map?
  - A) (5, 7)  B) (6, 4)  C) (2, 12)  D) (6, 12)
  - Answer: **D** — Dilation from origin: multiply each coordinate by scale factor. (2×3, 4×3) = (6, 12).

- **[F] D1** — Point A(3, 5) is translated 4 units right and 2 units down. What are the new coordinates?
  - A) (7, 3)  B) (7, 7)  C) (−1, 7)  D) (3, 3)
  - Answer: **A** — Translation: add 4 to x, subtract 2 from y. A' = (3+4, 5−2) = (7, 3).

- **[F] D1** — Point B(4, −3) is reflected over the x-axis. What are the new coordinates?
  - A) (−4, −3)  B) (4, 3)  C) (−4, 3)  D) (3, 4)
  - Answer: **B** — Reflection over x-axis: negate the y-coordinate. B' = (4, −(−3)) = (4, 3).

- **[F] D2** — Which transformation preserves both the shape and size of a figure?
  - A) Dilation with scale factor 2  B) Translation  C) Dilation with scale factor 1/2  D) Stretch
  - Answer: **B** — Translations (rigid motions) preserve both shape and size. Dilations change size.

- **[R] D4** — Which transformation maps △ABC onto itself (is a symmetry of the figure) if △ABC is equilateral?
  - A) Rotation of 90° about the centroid  B) Rotation of 120° about the centroid  C) Translation by any vector  D) Dilation by factor 2
  - Answer: **B** — An equilateral triangle has 3-fold rotational symmetry. Rotations of 120° and 240° about the centroid map it onto itself.

- **[R] D4** — A figure is reflected over the line x = 2. A point at (6, 3) maps to:
  - A) (−2, 3)  B) (−6, 3)  C) (−2, −3)  D) (2, 3)
  - Answer: **A** — Reflect over x = 2: distance from 6 to x=2 is 4. Mirror image is 4 units left of x=2: x = 2 − 4 = −2. Image: (−2, 3).

- **[R] D5** — Which sequence of transformations is equivalent to a rotation of 180° about the origin?
  - A) Reflection over x-axis then reflection over y-axis  B) Reflection over x-axis then translation right 2  C) Two consecutive translations  D) Dilation by −1 then rotation of 90°
  - Answer: **A** — Reflecting over x-axis: (x,y)→(x,−y). Then over y-axis: (x,−y)→(−x,−y). This is equivalent to 180° rotation about origin.

- **[U] D2** — Point C(2, 5) is reflected over the y-axis. What are the new coordinates?
  - A) (2, −5)  B) (−2, 5)  C) (−2, −5)  D) (5, 2)
  - Answer: **B** — Reflection over y-axis: negate the x-coordinate. C' = (−2, 5).

- **[U] D2** — Point D(3, 4) is rotated 90° counterclockwise about the origin. What are the new coordinates?
  - A) (4, 3)  B) (−4, 3)  C) (4, −3)  D) (−3, 4)
  - Answer: **B** — 90° CCW rotation: (x, y) → (−y, x). D' = (−4, 3).

- **[U] D3** — Point E(5, 3) is rotated 180° about the origin. What are the new coordinates?
  - A) (3, 5)  B) (−5, −3)  C) (5, −3)  D) (−3, −5)
  - Answer: **B** — 180° rotation about origin: (x, y) → (−x, −y). E' = (−5, −3).

---

### Precalculus (84 questions)


#### Analytic Trig

- **[A] D3** — Using the sum formula, find the exact value of sin(75°).
  - A) (√6 − √2)/4  B) (√6 + √2)/4  C) (√3 + 1)/4  D) √3/2
  - Answer: **B** — sin(75°) = sin(45° + 30°) = sin45 cos30 + cos45 sin30 = (√2/2)(√3/2) + (√2/2)(1/2) = √6/4 + √2/4 = (√6+√2)/4.

- **[A] D3** — If sin θ = 1/3 and θ is in Q I, find sin(2θ).
  - A) 2/9  B) 2√8/9  C) 4/9  D) √8/9
  - Answer: **B** — sin(2θ) = 2 sin θ cos θ. cos θ = √(1 − 1/9) = √(8/9) = 2√2/3. sin(2θ) = 2(1/3)(2√2/3) = 4√2/9 = 2√8/9. (4√2/9 ≡ 2√8/9 since √8 = 2√2.)

- **[A] D3** — Find the exact value of cos(π/8) using the half-angle formula.
  - A) √((1 + √2/2)/2)  B) √((2 + √2)/4)  C) √((1 − √2/2)/2)  D) (√6 + √2)/4
  - Answer: **B** — cos(π/8) = +√((1 + cos(π/4))/2) = √((1 + √2/2)/2) = √((2 + √2)/4). Option B matches.

- **[A] D4** — Solve: 2 sin²θ − sin θ − 1 = 0 for θ in [0, 2π).
  - A) θ = π/6, 5π/6  B) θ = π/2, 7π/6, 11π/6  C) θ = π/6, π/2, 5π/6  D) θ = 3π/2, π/6, 5π/6
  - Answer: **B** — Factor: (2 sin θ + 1)(sin θ − 1) = 0. sin θ = −1/2 → θ = 7π/6, 11π/6. sin θ = 1 → θ = π/2.

- **[F] D1** — Which is the Pythagorean identity?
  - A) sin²θ + cos²θ = 0  B) sin²θ + cos²θ = 1  C) sin²θ − cos²θ = 1  D) tan²θ + 1 = sin²θ
  - Answer: **B** — The fundamental Pythagorean identity is sin²θ + cos²θ = 1.

- **[F] D2** — What is the sum formula for sin(A + B)?
  - A) sin A cos B − cos A sin B  B) sin A cos B + cos A sin B  C) cos A cos B − sin A sin B  D) cos A cos B + sin A sin B
  - Answer: **B** — The sum formula: sin(A + B) = sin A cos B + cos A sin B.

- **[F] D2** — Solve for θ in [0, 2π): sin θ = 0.
  - A) θ = π/2, 3π/2  B) θ = 0, π  C) θ = 0, π/2, π, 3π/2  D) θ = π only
  - Answer: **B** — sin θ = 0 at θ = 0 and θ = π (in [0, 2π)).

- **[R] D4** — Which identity is used to derive the half-angle formula for sin(θ/2)?
  - A) cos(2θ) = 1 − 2sin²θ  B) sin(2θ) = 2 sin θ cos θ  C) tan(θ/2) = sin θ/(1 + cos θ)  D) cos²θ + sin²θ = 1
  - Answer: **A** — Starting from cos(2α) = 1 − 2sin²α, let α = θ/2: cos θ = 1 − 2sin²(θ/2) → sin²(θ/2) = (1 − cos θ)/2 → sin(θ/2) = ±√((1 − cos θ)/2).

- **[R] D4** — Simplify: (sin θ + cos θ)² using identities.
  - A) 1  B) 1 + sin(2θ)  C) 2 + 2 sin θ cos θ  D) sin²θ + cos²θ + 1
  - Answer: **B** — (sin θ + cos θ)² = sin²θ + 2 sin θ cos θ + cos²θ = 1 + 2 sin θ cos θ = 1 + sin(2θ).

- **[R] D5** — Which of the following is equivalent to cos(4θ)?
  - A) 4cos²θ − 1  B) 8cos⁴θ − 8cos²θ + 1  C) 4sin²θ cos²θ  D) 1 − 8sin²θ cos²θ
  - Answer: **B** — cos(4θ) = cos(2·2θ) = 2cos²(2θ)−1 = 2(2cos²θ−1)²−1 = 2(4cos⁴θ−4cos²θ+1)−1 = 8cos⁴θ−8cos²θ+1.

- **[U] D2** — Using the Pythagorean identity, simplify 1 − sin²θ.
  - A) tan²θ  B) sin²θ  C) cos²θ  D) cot²θ
  - Answer: **C** — From sin²θ + cos²θ = 1, we get 1 − sin²θ = cos²θ.

- **[U] D2** — What is the double-angle formula for cos(2θ)?
  - A) 2 sin θ cos θ  B) cos²θ − sin²θ  C) 1 − 2 cos²θ  D) sin²θ + cos²θ
  - Answer: **B** — cos(2θ) = cos²θ − sin²θ. (Equivalently 1 − 2sin²θ or 2cos²θ − 1.)

- **[U] D3** — Solve 2cos²θ − 1 = 0 for θ in [0, 2π).
  - A) θ = π/4, 3π/4, 5π/4, 7π/4  B) θ = π/3, 2π/3, 4π/3, 5π/3  C) θ = π/6, 5π/6, 7π/6, 11π/6  D) θ = π/4, 7π/4
  - Answer: **A** — 2cos²θ = 1 → cos²θ = 1/2 → cos θ = ±√2/2. Solutions: π/4, 3π/4, 5π/4, 7π/4.

- **[U] D3** — What is the difference formula for cos(A − B)?
  - A) cos A cos B − sin A sin B  B) cos A cos B + sin A sin B  C) sin A cos B + cos A sin B  D) sin A cos B − cos A sin B
  - Answer: **B** — cos(A − B) = cos A cos B + sin A sin B.


#### Exp Log

- **[A] D3** — A population starts at 500 and grows at 4% per year. Which model represents the population P after t years?
  - A) P = 500(0.04)ᵗ  B) P = 500 + 0.04t  C) P = 500(1.04)ᵗ  D) P = 500e^(0.4t)
  - Answer: **C** — Percent growth uses P = P₀(1 + r)ᵗ = 500(1.04)ᵗ.

- **[A] D3** — An investment doubles in 10 years with continuous compounding. What is the annual interest rate (to the nearest tenth)?
  - A) 6.9%  B) 7.2%  C) 5.0%  D) 10.0%
  - Answer: **A** — 2 = e^(10r) → ln 2 = 10r → r = ln2/10 ≈ 0.0693 ≈ 6.9%.

- **[A] D4** — A radioactive substance has a half-life of 20 years. What fraction remains after 60 years?
  - A) 1/4  B) 1/6  C) 1/8  D) 1/3
  - Answer: **C** — After 60 years = 3 half-lives. Fraction remaining = (1/2)³ = 1/8.

- **[F] D1** — Evaluate log₂(32).
  - A) 4  B) 5  C) 6  D) 16
  - Answer: **B** — 2⁵ = 32, so log₂(32) = 5.

- **[F] D2** — Solve for x: eˣ = 20.
  - A) x = ln(20)  B) x = log(20)  C) x = 20/e  D) x = e²⁰
  - Answer: **A** — Take the natural log of both sides: x = ln(20).

- **[F] D2** — What is the inverse function of f(x) = 3ˣ?
  - A) f⁻¹(x) = log₃(x)  B) f⁻¹(x) = x/3  C) f⁻¹(x) = 3/x  D) f⁻¹(x) = ln(3x)
  - Answer: **A** — The inverse of an exponential base 3 is the logarithm base 3: y = log₃(x).

- **[R] D4** — If log_a(2) = p and log_a(3) = q, express log_a(18) in terms of p and q.
  - A) p + q  B) p + 2q  C) 2p + q  D) pq
  - Answer: **B** — 18 = 2 × 3². So log_a(18) = log_a(2) + 2·log_a(3) = p + 2q.

- **[R] D5** — Solve: log₂(x) + log₂(x − 2) = 3.
  - A) x = 4  B) x = 2 or x = 4  C) x = −2 or x = 4  D) x = 3
  - Answer: **A** — log₂(x(x−2)) = 3 → x(x−2) = 8 → x²−2x−8 = 0 → (x−4)(x+2) = 0. x = 4 or −2. Since x > 2, only x = 4.

- **[R] D5** — Solve: 2^(2x) − 5·2^x + 4 = 0.
  - A) x = 0 and x = 2  B) x = 1 and x = 2  C) x = 0 and x = 1  D) x = 2 only
  - Answer: **C** — Let u = 2^x: u² − 5u + 4 = 0 → (u−1)(u−4) = 0. u = 1 → 2^x = 1 → x = 0. u = 4 → 2^x = 4 → x = 2. But check: 2^(2·2) − 5·4 + 4 = 16−20+4 = 0 ✓. x = 0 and x = 2. Wait—let u = 2^x, u=4→x=2, u=1→x=0. Correct: x = 0 and x = 2.

- **[U] D2** — Which expression equals log(a²b / c³)?
  - A) 2 log a + log b + 3 log c  B) 2 log a + log b − 3 log c  C) 2 log a − log b + 3 log c  D) log a + 2 log b − 3 log c
  - Answer: **B** — log(a²b/c³) = log(a²) + log(b) − log(c³) = 2 log a + log b − 3 log c.

- **[U] D2** — The logistic growth model levels off at a maximum population called the:
  - A) initial population  B) growth rate  C) carrying capacity  D) doubling time
  - Answer: **C** — In logistic growth P = K/(1 + Ae^(−rt)), the value K is the carrying capacity — the upper limit the population approaches.

- **[U] D3** — Solve: log₃(x − 1) = 2.
  - A) x = 7  B) x = 10  C) x = 9  D) x = 4
  - Answer: **B** — Convert: x − 1 = 3² = 9. Solve: x = 10.


#### Functions

- **[A] D3** — Find the inverse of f(x) = (x + 5) / 2.
  - A) f⁻¹(x) = 2x − 5  B) f⁻¹(x) = 2x + 5  C) f⁻¹(x) = (x − 5) / 2  D) f⁻¹(x) = x/2 + 5
  - Answer: **A** — Swap x and y: x = (y + 5)/2. Solve for y: 2x = y + 5, y = 2x − 5.

- **[A] D3** — A piecewise function is defined as f(x) = {x² if x < 0; 2x + 1 if x ≥ 0}. What is f(−2) + f(3)?
  - A) 9  B) 11  C) 7  D) 4
  - Answer: **B** — f(−2) = (−2)² = 4. f(3) = 2(3) + 1 = 7. Sum = 4 + 7 = 11.

- **[A] D4** — If f(x) = √(x + 1) and g(x) = x², find the domain of (f ∘ g)(x).
  - A) x ≥ 0  B) all real numbers  C) x ≥ −1  D) x > 0
  - Answer: **B** — f(g(x)) = √(x² + 1). Since x² ≥ 0, x² + 1 ≥ 1 > 0 for all real x. Domain is all reals.

- **[F] D1** — What is the domain of f(x) = √(x − 3)?
  - A) x > 3  B) x ≥ 3  C) x < 3  D) all real numbers
  - Answer: **B** — The radicand must be non-negative: x − 3 ≥ 0, so x ≥ 3.

- **[F] D1** — Given g(x) = 2x − 4, what is g(3)?
  - A) 2  B) 6  C) 10  D) 2
  - Answer: **A** — g(3) = 2(3) − 4 = 6 − 4 = 2.

- **[F] D2** — What is the range of f(x) = |x| − 1?
  - A) y ≥ 0  B) y ≥ −1  C) all real numbers  D) y > −1
  - Answer: **B** — |x| ≥ 0 for all x, so |x| − 1 ≥ −1. The range is y ≥ −1.

- **[R] D4** — Which function is even?
  - A) f(x) = x³ + x  B) f(x) = x² + x  C) f(x) = x⁴ − 2x²  D) f(x) = x³ − x²
  - Answer: **C** — An even function satisfies f(−x) = f(x). f(−x) = (−x)⁴ − 2(−x)² = x⁴ − 2x² = f(x). ✓

- **[R] D4** — The graph of f(x) is shifted 3 units left and reflected over the x-axis. Which expression represents this transformation?
  - A) −f(x − 3)  B) −f(x + 3)  C) f(−x + 3)  D) f(−x − 3)
  - Answer: **B** — Shift left 3: f(x + 3). Reflect over x-axis: −f(x + 3).

- **[R] D5** — Which statement correctly describes an odd function?
  - A) Its graph is symmetric about the y-axis  B) f(−x) = f(x) for all x in the domain  C) Its graph is symmetric about the origin  D) f(0) must equal 0
  - Answer: **C** — An odd function satisfies f(−x) = −f(x), which means rotational symmetry about the origin. A requires f(−x) = f(x) (even), B is the definition of even, D is not always true.

- **[U] D2** — If f(x) = x² + 1, what is f(x + 2)?
  - A) x² + 5  B) x² + 4x + 5  C) x² + 2x + 5  D) x² + 4x + 3
  - Answer: **B** — f(x + 2) = (x + 2)² + 1 = x² + 4x + 4 + 1 = x² + 4x + 5.

- **[U] D2** — If f(x) = 3x and g(x) = x + 2, what is (f ∘ g)(1)?
  - A) 5  B) 9  C) 7  D) 3
  - Answer: **B** — g(1) = 1 + 2 = 3. Then f(g(1)) = f(3) = 3(3) = 9.

- **[U] D3** — If f(x) = 2x + 1 and g(x) = x − 3, what is (g ∘ f)(x)?
  - A) 2x − 2  B) 2x − 5  C) 2x + 4  D) 2x − 1
  - Answer: **A** — g(f(x)) = g(2x + 1) = (2x + 1) − 3 = 2x − 2.


#### Limits Intro

- **[A] D3** — Evaluate lim(x→2) (x² − 4) / (x − 2).
  - A) 0  B) undefined  C) 2  D) 4
  - Answer: **D** — Factor: (x−2)(x+2)/(x−2) = x + 2. As x→2, x + 2 → 4.

- **[A] D3** — Use the graph to determine lim(x→2) f(x) given that f approaches 5 from the left and from the right as x→2, but f(2) = 3.
  - A) 3  B) 5  C) undefined  D) does not exist
  - Answer: **B** — The limit depends on what f approaches, not the value at the point. Both sides approach 5, so the limit is 5.

- **[A] D4** — Evaluate lim(x→0) (1 − cos x) / x.
  - A) 1  B) 0  C) undefined  D) 1/2
  - Answer: **B** — Using the standard limit lim(x→0)(1 − cos x)/x = 0. (This can be verified numerically or by L'Hôpital's rule.)

- **[F] D1** — What does lim(x→3) (x + 2) equal?
  - A) 2  B) 3  C) 5  D) undefined
  - Answer: **C** — Direct substitution: 3 + 2 = 5.

- **[F] D2** — Evaluate lim(x→0) (sin x / x) numerically or by rule.
  - A) 0  B) undefined  C) 1  D) ∞
  - Answer: **C** — This is a fundamental limit: lim(x→0) sin(x)/x = 1.

- **[R] D4** — A function f has a removable discontinuity at x = c if:
  - A) lim(x→c) f(x) = ∞  B) f(c) is undefined but lim(x→c) f(x) exists and is finite  C) The left and right limits are different  D) f(c) is defined but not equal to the limit
  - Answer: **B** — Removable discontinuity: the limit exists (finite) but f(c) is undefined (or defined but different). The 'hole' can be 'filled.'

- **[R] D5** — Evaluate lim(x→∞) (3x² + 2) / (x² − 5).
  - A) 0  B) ∞  C) 3  D) 2/5
  - Answer: **C** — Divide numerator and denominator by x²: (3 + 2/x²)/(1 − 5/x²). As x→∞, terms with 1/x²→0. Limit = 3/1 = 3.

- **[U] D2** — Which best describes what lim(x→a) f(x) = L means?
  - A) f(a) = L  B) As x gets close to a, f(x) gets close to L  C) f(x) = L when x = a  D) f is defined at x = a and equals L
  - Answer: **B** — A limit describes the behavior of f as x approaches a, not necessarily the value at a.

- **[U] D2** — A function is continuous at x = a if:
  - A) lim(x→a) f(x) exists  B) f(a) is defined  C) f(a) is defined, lim(x→a) f(x) exists, and they are equal  D) The function has no vertical asymptote at x = a
  - Answer: **C** — Continuity requires all three: f(a) defined, limit exists, and the limit equals f(a).

- **[U] D3** — If lim(x→3⁻) f(x) = 4 and lim(x→3⁺) f(x) = 7, then lim(x→3) f(x):
  - A) equals 4  B) equals 7  C) equals 5.5  D) does not exist
  - Answer: **D** — A limit exists only if both one-sided limits are equal. Since 4 ≠ 7, the two-sided limit does not exist.


#### Polar Vectors

- **[A] D3** — A parametric curve is given by x = 2t and y = t² − 1. What is the rectangular equation?
  - A) y = x² − 1  B) y = x²/4 − 1  C) y = (x/2)²  D) y = 4x² − 1
  - Answer: **B** — t = x/2. Substitute: y = (x/2)² − 1 = x²/4 − 1.

- **[A] D3** — A plane flies at 200 mph heading N 60° E. Find the eastward component of its velocity.
  - A) 100 mph  B) 100√3 mph  C) 173 mph  D) 200 mph
  - Answer: **C** — Eastward = 200 sin(60°) = 200(√3/2) ≈ 173 mph.

- **[A] D4** — A parametric path is: x = cos t, y = sin t for 0 ≤ t ≤ 2π. What curve does it trace?
  - A) A line  B) An ellipse  C) A unit circle  D) A parabola
  - Answer: **C** — x² + y² = cos²t + sin²t = 1. This is the unit circle.

- **[F] D1** — Convert the polar point (4, π/3) to rectangular coordinates.
  - A) (2√3, 2)  B) (2, 2√3)  C) (4, 4√3)  D) (√3, 1)
  - Answer: **B** — x = r cos θ = 4 cos(π/3) = 4(1/2) = 2. y = r sin θ = 4 sin(π/3) = 4(√3/2) = 2√3. Point: (2, 2√3).

- **[F] D2** — The vector u = ⟨3, 4⟩. What is its magnitude?
  - A) 7  B) √7  C) 5  D) 25
  - Answer: **C** — |u| = √(3² + 4²) = √(9 + 16) = √25 = 5.

- **[R] D4** — Two vectors u and v are perpendicular if and only if:
  - A) |u| = |v|  B) u · v = 0  C) u · v = 1  D) u + v = 0
  - Answer: **B** — Two vectors are perpendicular (orthogonal) if and only if their dot product equals 0.

- **[R] D5** — The polar curve r = 1 + cos θ is called a:
  - A) Lemniscate  B) Rose curve  C) Cardioid  D) Limaçon without inner loop
  - Answer: **C** — r = 1 + cos θ is a cardioid — a heart-shaped curve where the coefficient of the trig term equals the constant.

- **[U] D2** — Convert the rectangular point (3, −3) to polar form (r, θ) with r > 0 and 0 ≤ θ < 2π.
  - A) (3√2, π/4)  B) (3√2, 7π/4)  C) (3, 7π/4)  D) (√18, π/4)
  - Answer: **B** — r = √(9+9) = 3√2. θ: x > 0, y < 0 → Q IV. tan θ = −1 → θ = 7π/4.

- **[U] D2** — Find the dot product of u = ⟨2, −1⟩ and v = ⟨4, 3⟩.
  - A) 11  B) 5  C) −5  D) 8
  - Answer: **B** — u · v = (2)(4) + (−1)(3) = 8 − 3 = 5.

- **[U] D3** — The polar equation r = 3 represents:
  - A) A horizontal line at y = 3  B) A vertical line at x = 3  C) A circle of radius 3 centered at the origin  D) A line through the origin
  - Answer: **C** — r = constant is a circle centered at the origin with radius equal to that constant.


#### Poly Rational

- **[A] D3** — Identify any holes in f(x) = (x² − 4) / (x − 2).
  - A) Hole at x = 2  B) Vertical asymptote at x = 2  C) Hole at x = −2  D) No holes
  - Answer: **A** — Factor numerator: (x−2)(x+2)/(x−2). Cancel common factor → hole at x = 2, not an asymptote.

- **[A] D3** — Find the horizontal asymptote of f(x) = (3x² + 1) / (x² − 5).
  - A) y = 0  B) y = 3  C) y = 1/5  D) No horizontal asymptote
  - Answer: **B** — Degrees are equal (both 2). HA = ratio of leading coefficients = 3/1 = 3.

- **[A] D4** — Find all vertical asymptotes of f(x) = (x + 1) / (x² − x − 6).
  - A) x = 3 only  B) x = −2 only  C) x = 3 and x = −2  D) x = 1 and x = −1
  - Answer: **C** — Denom: (x−3)(x+2). Neither factor cancels with (x+1). Vertical asymptotes at x = 3 and x = −2.

- **[F] D1** — What are the zeros of f(x) = (x − 2)(x + 5)?
  - A) x = −2, x = 5  B) x = 2, x = −5  C) x = 2, x = 5  D) x = −2, x = −5
  - Answer: **B** — Set each factor to zero: x − 2 = 0 → x = 2; x + 5 = 0 → x = −5.

- **[F] D1** — How many complex zeros (counting multiplicity) does a degree-5 polynomial have?
  - A) At most 5  B) Exactly 5  C) At most 4  D) Exactly 3
  - Answer: **B** — By the Fundamental Theorem of Algebra, a degree-n polynomial has exactly n complex zeros counting multiplicity.

- **[F] D2** — Find the vertical asymptote(s) of f(x) = 1 / (x − 4).
  - A) x = 1  B) x = −4  C) x = 4  D) x = 0
  - Answer: **C** — Vertical asymptotes occur where the denominator equals zero: x − 4 = 0 → x = 4.

- **[R] D4** — The polynomial p(x) has degree 4 with a positive leading coefficient. The graph bounces off the x-axis at x = 1 and crosses at x = −2. What can you conclude?
  - A) x = 1 is a simple zero; x = −2 is a repeated zero  B) x = 1 is a repeated zero (even multiplicity); x = −2 is a simple zero  C) Both zeros have multiplicity 2  D) x = 1 has multiplicity 3; x = −2 has multiplicity 1
  - Answer: **B** — Bouncing off (touching) indicates even multiplicity; crossing indicates odd multiplicity.

- **[R] D5** — If 3 + 2i is a zero of a polynomial with real coefficients, what other zero must exist?
  - A) 3 − 2i  B) −3 + 2i  C) 2 + 3i  D) −3 − 2i
  - Answer: **A** — Complex zeros of polynomials with real coefficients come in conjugate pairs. The conjugate of 3 + 2i is 3 − 2i.

- **[R] D5** — A rational function has a slant asymptote when the degree of the numerator is exactly one more than the degree of the denominator. What is the slant asymptote of f(x) = (x² + 3x + 1) / (x + 1)?
  - A) y = x + 2  B) y = x + 4  C) y = x − 2  D) y = x
  - Answer: **A** — Divide x² + 3x + 1 by x + 1 using polynomial long division: x + 2 remainder −1. Slant asymptote: y = x + 2.

- **[U] D2** — What is the end behavior of f(x) = −2x³ + 5x as x → +∞?
  - A) f(x) → +∞  B) f(x) → −∞  C) f(x) → 0  D) f(x) → 2
  - Answer: **B** — Leading term is −2x³. Odd degree, negative leading coefficient: as x → +∞, f(x) → −∞.

- **[U] D2** — Which best describes the graph of f(x) = x⁴ − 3x² + 2 as x → −∞?
  - A) f(x) → −∞  B) f(x) → +∞  C) f(x) → 0  D) f(x) → −3
  - Answer: **B** — Leading term x⁴ (even degree, positive). Both ends go to +∞.

- **[U] D3** — Simplify: (x² + 2x − 8) / (x² + x − 6), stating any restrictions.
  - A) (x + 4)/(x + 3), x ≠ 2 and x ≠ −3  B) (x − 2)/(x − 3), x ≠ −4  C) (x + 4)/(x + 3), x ≠ 3  D) (x − 4)/(x − 3), x ≠ 2
  - Answer: **A** — Num: (x+4)(x−2). Denom: (x+3)(x−2). Cancel (x−2): (x+4)/(x+3). Restrictions: x ≠ 2 and x ≠ −3.


#### Trig Functions

- **[A] D3** — What is the period of f(x) = sin(3x)?
  - A) π/3  B) 3π  C) 2π/3  D) 6π
  - Answer: **C** — Period = 2π / |B| = 2π / 3.

- **[A] D3** — What is the amplitude of f(x) = −4 cos(x)?
  - A) −4  B) 1/4  C) 4  D) 2
  - Answer: **C** — Amplitude = |A| = |−4| = 4. Amplitude is always non-negative.

- **[A] D3** — A Ferris wheel of radius 20 m has its center 25 m above the ground. If it completes one rotation in 40 seconds, which function models the height h(t)?
  - A) h(t) = 20 sin(π/20 · t) + 25  B) h(t) = 25 sin(π/20 · t) + 20  C) h(t) = 20 cos(2π/40 · t) + 25  D) h(t) = 20 sin(40t) + 25
  - Answer: **C** — Amplitude = 20 (radius). Vertical shift = 25 (center height). Period = 40 → B = 2π/40 = π/20. Using cosine: h(t) = 20 cos(π/20 · t) + 25. Option C matches.

- **[F] D1** — What is sin(π/2)?
  - A) 0  B) 1  C) √2/2  D) 1/2
  - Answer: **B** — On the unit circle, the point at π/2 (90°) is (0, 1), so sin(π/2) = 1.

- **[F] D1** — What is cos(π)?
  - A) 1  B) 0  C) −1  D) √3/2
  - Answer: **C** — At π (180°), the point on the unit circle is (−1, 0), so cos(π) = −1.

- **[F] D2** — Evaluate tan(π/4).
  - A) 0  B) 1  C) √3  D) 1/√2
  - Answer: **B** — tan(π/4) = sin(π/4)/cos(π/4) = (√2/2)/(√2/2) = 1.

- **[F] D2** — What is the exact value of cos(5π/6)?
  - A) √3/2  B) −√3/2  C) 1/2  D) −1/2
  - Answer: **B** — 5π/6 is in Q II; reference angle π/6. cos(π/6) = √3/2, and cosine is negative in Q II: −√3/2.

- **[R] D4** — What is the phase shift of f(x) = sin(2x − π/3)?
  - A) π/3 to the right  B) π/6 to the right  C) 2π/3 to the right  D) π/3 to the left
  - Answer: **B** — f(x) = sin(2(x − π/6)). Phase shift = π/6 to the right.

- **[R] D4** — Which of the following has a period of π?
  - A) y = sin(x)  B) y = tan(x)  C) y = cos(2x)  D) y = sin(2x)
  - Answer: **B** — tan(x) has a natural period of π. cos(2x) and sin(2x) also have period π, but the question asks which has a period of π among these choices. Both B and C/D do — but tan(x) is the classic answer. Since tan(x) naturally has period π (B), and sin(2x)/cos(2x) also qualify, the best single answer for 'inherently has period π' is tan(x).

- **[R] D5** — The graph of y = A sin(Bx + C) + D has amplitude 3, period 4π, phase shift π/2 to the left, and midline y = −1. Which equation matches?
  - A) y = 3 sin(x/2 + π/4) − 1  B) y = 3 sin(x/2 + π/2) − 1  C) y = 3 sin(2x + π/2) − 1  D) y = 3 sin(x/2 − π/2) − 1
  - Answer: **B** — A=3, period 4π→B=2π/4π=1/2. Phase shift left π/2: C/B = π/2 → C = π/4... Wait: y = A sin(B(x + shift))+D = 3 sin((1/2)(x + π/2)) − 1 = 3 sin(x/2 + π/4) − 1. That's option A. Rechecking: phase shift = −C/B = π/2 → C = Bπ/2 = (1/2)(π/2) = π/4. So y = 3 sin(x/2 + π/4) − 1. Answer A.

- **[U] D2** — Which quadrant contains an angle where sin θ > 0 and cos θ < 0?
  - A) Quadrant I  B) Quadrant II  C) Quadrant III  D) Quadrant IV
  - Answer: **B** — sin > 0 means y > 0 (Q I or II). cos < 0 means x < 0 (Q II or III). Intersection: Quadrant II.

- **[U] D2** — If sin θ = 3/5 and θ is in Quadrant I, what is cos θ?
  - A) 4/5  B) 3/4  C) 5/4  D) √34/5
  - Answer: **A** — Pythagorean identity: cos²θ = 1 − sin²θ = 1 − 9/25 = 16/25. In Q I, cos θ = 4/5.

- **[U] D3** — Csc(θ) is defined as:
  - A) cos θ / sin θ  B) 1 / cos θ  C) 1 / sin θ  D) sin θ / cos θ
  - Answer: **C** — Cosecant is the reciprocal of sine: csc θ = 1 / sin θ.

- **[U] D3** — If sec θ = 2, what is cos θ?
  - A) 2  B) −1/2  C) 1/2  D) √2
  - Answer: **C** — sec θ = 1/cos θ = 2, so cos θ = 1/2.

---

### SAT Math (150 questions)


#### Additional Topics

- **[A] D2** — A ladder 10 feet long leans against a wall. The foot of the ladder is 6 feet from the wall. How high up the wall does the ladder reach?
  - A) 4 feet  B) 6 feet  C) 8 feet  D) √136 feet
  - Answer: **C** — Height = √(10² − 6²) = √(100 − 36) = √64 = 8 feet.

- **[A] D3** — A cylindrical can has radius 3 cm and height 10 cm. What is its volume?
  - A) 30π cm³  B) 60π cm³  C) 90π cm³  D) 300π cm³
  - Answer: **C** — Volume = πr²h = π(9)(10) = 90π cm³.

- **[A] D3** — A kite string makes a 30° angle with the ground. If 60 feet of string are out, how high is the kite?
  - A) 20 feet  B) 30 feet  C) 30√3 feet  D) 60 feet
  - Answer: **B** — Height = 60 × sin(30°) = 60 × (1/2) = 30 feet.

- **[A] D4** — A park is shaped like a circle with diameter 100 meters. What is its area to the nearest square meter? (π ≈ 3.14)
  - A) 314 m²  B) 3,140 m²  C) 7,850 m²  D) 31,400 m²
  - Answer: **C** — Radius = 50 m. Area = π × 50² = 3.14 × 2,500 = 7,850 m².

- **[A] D4** — A ramp rises 4 feet over a horizontal run of 20 feet. What angle does the ramp make with the ground? (Use tan⁻¹)
  - A) tan⁻¹(1/5)  B) tan⁻¹(4)  C) tan⁻¹(5)  D) tan⁻¹(1/4)
  - Answer: **A** — tan(θ) = opposite/adjacent = 4/20 = 1/5. Angle = tan⁻¹(1/5).

- **[A] D5** — A sphere has a volume of 36π cm³. What is its radius?
  - A) 2  B) 3  C) 4  D) 6
  - Answer: **B** — V = (4/3)πr³ = 36π → r³ = 27 → r = 3.

- **[F] D1** — What is the area of a triangle with base 10 and height 6?
  - A) 16  B) 30  C) 60  D) 120
  - Answer: **B** — Area = (1/2) × base × height = (1/2)(10)(6) = 30.

- **[F] D1** — What is sin(30°)?
  - A) √3/2  B) 1/2  C) √2/2  D) 1
  - Answer: **B** — sin(30°) = 1/2 (standard unit circle value).

- **[F] D2** — What is the circumference of a circle with radius 5? (Use π)
  - A) 5π  B) 10π  C) 25π  D) 50π
  - Answer: **B** — Circumference = 2πr = 2π(5) = 10π.

- **[F] D2** — In a right triangle, the two legs are 3 and 4. What is the hypotenuse?
  - A) 5  B) 7  C) √7  D) 12
  - Answer: **A** — By the Pythagorean theorem: c² = 9 + 16 = 25, so c = 5.

- **[F] D3** — What is the area of a circle with diameter 12?
  - A) 12π  B) 24π  C) 36π  D) 144π
  - Answer: **C** — Radius = 6. Area = πr² = π(36) = 36π.

- **[F] D3** — In a right triangle, sin(θ) = 3/5. What is cos(θ)?
  - A) 4/5  B) 3/4  C) 5/3  D) 1/5
  - Answer: **A** — Using Pythagorean identity: cos²θ = 1 − sin²θ = 1 − 9/25 = 16/25. cosθ = 4/5.

- **[F] D4** — What is the value of i + i² + i³ + i⁴, where i = √(−1)?
  - A) 0  B) 1  C) i  D) 2i
  - Answer: **A** — i = i, i² = −1, i³ = −i, i⁴ = 1. Sum = i + (−1) + (−i) + 1 = 0.

- **[R] D2** — Triangle ABC is similar to triangle DEF. If AB = 6, DE = 9, and BC = 8, what is EF?
  - A) 10  B) 11  C) 12  D) 54
  - Answer: **C** — Scale factor = DE/AB = 9/6 = 3/2. EF = BC × (3/2) = 8 × 1.5 = 12.

- **[R] D3** — An arc of a circle has a central angle of 120° and the radius is 6. What is the arc length?
  - A) 2π  B) 3π  C) 4π  D) 12π
  - Answer: **C** — Arc length = (θ/360°) × 2πr = (120/360) × 2π(6) = (1/3)(12π) = 4π.

- **[R] D3** — If (3 + 2i) + (1 − 5i) = a + bi, what are a and b?
  - A) a = 4, b = −3  B) a = 4, b = 3  C) a = 2, b = −3  D) a = 3, b = −7
  - Answer: **A** — (3+1) + (2−5)i = 4 + (−3)i. So a = 4, b = −3.

- **[R] D4** — A rectangle has a diagonal of 13 cm and one side of 5 cm. What is the other side?
  - A) 8  B) 10  C) 12  D) √194
  - Answer: **C** — Using Pythagorean theorem: other side = √(13² − 5²) = √(169 − 25) = √144 = 12.

- **[R] D4** — What is the product (2 + 3i)(2 − 3i)?
  - A) 4 − 9i²  B) 4 + 9  C) 13  D) −5
  - Answer: **C** — (2 + 3i)(2 − 3i) = 4 − 9i² = 4 − 9(−1) = 4 + 9 = 13.

- **[R] D5** — In a right triangle, one acute angle is twice the other. What are the two acute angles?
  - A) 30° and 60°  B) 40° and 80°  C) 45° and 45°  D) 25° and 75°
  - Answer: **A** — Two acute angles sum to 90°. Let one angle = x, other = 2x. x + 2x = 90° → x = 30°. Angles: 30° and 60°.

- **[U] D2** — Two angles of a triangle measure 55° and 75°. What is the third angle?
  - A) 40°  B) 50°  C) 60°  D) 70°
  - Answer: **B** — Sum of angles in a triangle = 180°. Third angle = 180° − 55° − 75° = 50°.

- **[U] D3** — A circle has a central angle of 90°. What fraction of the circle's area does the corresponding sector represent?
  - A) 1/2  B) 1/3  C) 1/4  D) 1/8
  - Answer: **C** — 90°/360° = 1/4 of the circle's area.

- **[U] D3** — What is the relationship between sin(θ) and cos(90° − θ)?
  - A) They are negatives of each other  B) They are equal  C) sin(θ) is twice cos(90° − θ)  D) They are reciprocals
  - Answer: **B** — Co-function identity: sin(θ) = cos(90° − θ). They are equal.

- **[U] D4** — What is i⁴ + i⁸ + i¹²?
  - A) 0  B) 3  C) −3  D) 3i
  - Answer: **B** — i⁴ = 1, i⁸ = (i⁴)² = 1, i¹² = (i⁴)³ = 1. Sum = 1 + 1 + 1 = 3.

- **[U] D4** — In the coordinate plane, point A is at (1, 2) and B is at (4, 6). What is the length of AB?
  - A) 3  B) 4  C) 5  D) 7
  - Answer: **C** — Distance = √((4−1)² + (6−2)²) = √(9 + 16) = √25 = 5.

- **[U] D5** — In a right triangle with legs a and b and hypotenuse c, which relationship is always true?
  - A) a + b = c  B) a² + b² = c²  C) a² − b² = c²  D) 2ab = c²
  - Answer: **B** — The Pythagorean theorem states a² + b² = c² for any right triangle.


#### Heart Of Algebra

- **[A] D1** — Maria earns $15 per hour. She worked h hours. Which expression gives her total earnings?
  - A) h + 15  B) h − 15  C) 15h  D) h/15
  - Answer: **C** — Total earnings = rate × hours = 15h.

- **[A] D2** — A taxi charges a flat fee of $3 plus $2 per mile. If a ride costs $17, how many miles was the ride?
  - A) 5  B) 7  C) 8  D) 10
  - Answer: **B** — 3 + 2m = 17 → 2m = 14 → m = 7.

- **[A] D2** — A store sells pens for $2 each and notebooks for $5 each. James buys 4 pens and n notebooks and spends $28. How many notebooks did he buy?
  - A) 3  B) 4  C) 5  D) 6
  - Answer: **B** — 2(4) + 5n = 28 → 8 + 5n = 28 → 5n = 20 → n = 4.

- **[A] D3** — The sum of two numbers is 50, and one number is 8 more than the other. What is the smaller number?
  - A) 19  B) 21  C) 29  D) 31
  - Answer: **B** — x + (x + 8) = 50 → 2x + 8 = 50 → 2x = 42 → x = 21.

- **[A] D3** — A car rental company charges $30 per day plus $0.20 per mile. If Ana's bill is $86 for a 1-day rental, how many miles did she drive?
  - A) 230  B) 280  C) 300  D) 430
  - Answer: **B** — 30 + 0.20m = 86 → 0.20m = 56 → m = 280.

- **[A] D3** — A school needs to order at least 200 chairs. They already have 75. Each classroom requires 25 chairs. What is the minimum number of classrooms' worth of chairs they need to order?
  - A) 5  B) 6  C) 7  D) 8
  - Answer: **A** — 75 + 25c ≥ 200 → 25c ≥ 125 → c ≥ 5. Minimum is 5.

- **[A] D4** — Two friends start 120 miles apart and drive toward each other. One drives 40 mph and the other drives 60 mph. After how many hours do they meet?
  - A) 1  B) 1.2  C) 1.5  D) 2
  - Answer: **B** — Combined speed = 100 mph. Time = 120/100 = 1.2 hours.

- **[A] D4** — A plumber charges $50 for the first hour and $40 for each additional hour. If a job costs $210, how many total hours did the plumber work?
  - A) 3  B) 4  C) 5  D) 6
  - Answer: **C** — 50 + 40(h − 1) = 210 → 40(h−1) = 160 → h − 1 = 4 → h = 5.

- **[A] D4** — A gym has two membership plans. Plan A: $25/month. Plan B: $10 upfront + $20/month. After how many months is Plan B cheaper than Plan A?
  - A) 1  B) 2  C) 3  D) 4
  - Answer: **B** — Plan B < Plan A: 10 + 20m < 25m → 10 < 5m → m > 2. So after 2 months (from month 3 onward), Plan B is cheaper.

- **[A] D5** — A truck driver needs to deliver goods at least 400 miles away. He can travel at most 65 mph and has at most 7 hours of drive time. If the trip is exactly d miles, which system describes feasible values of d and time t?
  - A) d ≥ 400, t ≤ 7, d ≤ 65t  B) d ≥ 400, t ≥ 7, d = 65t  C) d ≤ 400, t ≤ 7, d ≤ 65t  D) d ≥ 400, t ≤ 7, d ≥ 65t
  - Answer: **A** — Must cover at least 400 miles (d ≥ 400), within 7 hours (t ≤ 7), at no more than 65 mph (d ≤ 65t).

- **[F] D1** — What is the value of x if 3x = 18?
  - A) 3  B) 5  C) 6  D) 9
  - Answer: **C** — Divide both sides by 3: x = 18 / 3 = 6.

- **[F] D1** — Solve for y: y + 7 = 15.
  - A) 6  B) 7  C) 8  D) 22
  - Answer: **C** — Subtract 7 from both sides: y = 15 − 7 = 8.

- **[F] D2** — If 2x − 5 = 11, what is x?
  - A) 3  B) 6  C) 8  D) 16
  - Answer: **C** — Add 5 to both sides: 2x = 16. Divide by 2: x = 8.

- **[F] D2** — Which value of x satisfies 4x + 3 = 19?
  - A) 2  B) 3  C) 4  D) 5
  - Answer: **C** — Subtract 3: 4x = 16. Divide by 4: x = 4.

- **[F] D2** — What is the slope of the line 2x − 4y = 8?
  - A) −2  B) 1/2  C) 2  D) 4
  - Answer: **B** — Rewrite in slope-intercept form: y = (1/2)x − 2. Slope = 1/2.

- **[F] D2** — What is the y-intercept of the line y = 3x − 7?
  - A) −7  B) 3  C) 7  D) −3
  - Answer: **A** — The y-intercept is the constant term in y = mx + b form: −7.

- **[F] D2** — If 5(x − 2) = 20, what is x?
  - A) 2  B) 4  C) 6  D) 22
  - Answer: **C** — Divide both sides by 5: x − 2 = 4. Add 2: x = 6.

- **[F] D3** — Solve the system: x + y = 10 and x − y = 4. What is x?
  - A) 3  B) 5  C) 7  D) 14
  - Answer: **C** — Add the two equations: 2x = 14, so x = 7.

- **[F] D3** — Which inequality represents 'x is at least 5'?
  - A) x < 5  B) x > 5  C) x ≤ 5  D) x ≥ 5
  - Answer: **D** — 'At least 5' means x is greater than or equal to 5, so x ≥ 5.

- **[F] D3** — If 3x + 2y = 12 and y = 3, what is x?
  - A) 1  B) 2  C) 3  D) 4
  - Answer: **B** — Substitute y = 3: 3x + 6 = 12, so 3x = 6, x = 2.

- **[F] D3** — What is the x-intercept of the line y = 2x − 6?
  - A) −3  B) 3  C) 6  D) −6
  - Answer: **B** — Set y = 0: 0 = 2x − 6, so x = 3.

- **[F] D4** — Solve for x: (x/3) + (x/6) = 5.
  - A) 6  B) 9  C) 10  D) 15
  - Answer: **C** — Multiply through by 6: 2x + x = 30, so 3x = 30, x = 10.

- **[F] D4** — What is the solution to |2x − 3| = 7?
  - A) x = 5 only  B) x = −2 only  C) x = 5 or x = −2  D) x = 2 or x = −5
  - Answer: **C** — 2x − 3 = 7 → x = 5; 2x − 3 = −7 → 2x = −4 → x = −2.

- **[F] D4** — Line ℓ passes through (0, 4) and (2, 0). What is the equation of ℓ?
  - A) y = 2x + 4  B) y = −2x + 4  C) y = −2x − 4  D) y = 2x − 4
  - Answer: **B** — Slope = (0 − 4)/(2 − 0) = −2. y-intercept = 4. Equation: y = −2x + 4.

- **[F] D5** — If ax + by = c and bx − ay = d, what is x + y in terms of a, b, c, d?
  - A) (c + d)/(a + b)  B) (c − d)/(a − b)  C) (c + d)/(a² + b²) × (a + b)  D) (ac + bd)/(a² + b²)
  - Answer: **C** — Multiply eq1 by (a+b) and add strategically: x + y = (c+d)(a+b)/(a²+b²).

- **[R] D2** — If f(x) = 3x − 5 and f(a) = 7, what is the value of a?
  - A) 2  B) 3  C) 4  D) 6
  - Answer: **C** — 3a − 5 = 7 → 3a = 12 → a = 4.

- **[R] D3** — The graph of y = mx + b passes through (−2, 1) and (4, 13). What is m + b?
  - A) 3  B) 5  C) 7  D) 9
  - Answer: **C** — Slope m = (13−1)/(4−(−2)) = 12/6 = 2. Using (4,13): 13 = 8 + b → b = 5. m + b = 7.

- **[R] D3** — If 4 − 3x > 10, which of the following could be x?
  - A) −3  B) −1  C) 0  D) 2
  - Answer: **A** — 4 − 3x > 10 → −3x > 6 → x < −2. Only −3 satisfies x < −2.

- **[R] D3** — If 2a − b = 5 and a + b = 10, what is the value of 3a?
  - A) 5  B) 10  C) 15  D) 20
  - Answer: **C** — Add the equations: 3a = 15, so 3a = 15.

- **[R] D4** — A line is graphed in the xy-plane. The line passes through (0, 5) and has slope −2. At what x-value does the line cross y = −3?
  - A) 1  B) 2  C) 3  D) 4
  - Answer: **D** — y = −2x + 5. Set −3 = −2x + 5 → −2x = −8 → x = 4.

- **[R] D4** — Which of the following systems has exactly one solution?
  - A) y = 2x + 1 and 2y = 4x + 2  B) y = 3x − 4 and y = 3x + 7  C) y = x + 5 and y = −x + 3  D) y = 2x and 4x − 2y = 0
  - Answer: **C** — Option C: x + 5 = −x + 3 → 2x = −2 → x = −1. Unique intersection.

- **[R] D4** — The sum of three consecutive integers is 66. What is the largest of the three?
  - A) 21  B) 22  C) 23  D) 24
  - Answer: **C** — n + (n+1) + (n+2) = 66 → 3n + 3 = 66 → n = 21. Largest = 23.

- **[R] D4** — What is the value of x + y if 3x + y = 14 and x + 3y = 10?
  - A) 4  B) 5  C) 6  D) 8
  - Answer: **C** — Add the equations: 4x + 4y = 24 → x + y = 6.

- **[R] D5** — In the xy-plane, the line with equation ax − 2y = 8 has an x-intercept of 4. What is a?
  - A) 1  B) 2  C) 3  D) 4
  - Answer: **B** — At the x-intercept, y = 0: a(4) − 0 = 8 → 4a = 8 → a = 2.

- **[R] D5** — If |3x − 6| < 9, which of the following describes all solutions?
  - A) −1 < x < 5  B) x > −1 or x < 5  C) −1 < x < 5 is wrong; −3 < x < 5  D) x < −1 or x > 5
  - Answer: **A** — −9 < 3x − 6 < 9 → −3 < 3x < 15 → −1 < x < 5.

- **[U] D2** — A line has a negative slope and a positive y-intercept. Which quadrant does it NOT pass through?
  - A) Quadrant I  B) Quadrant II  C) Quadrant III  D) Quadrant IV
  - Answer: **C** — A line y = mx + b with m < 0 and b > 0 passes through Q I, Q II, Q IV — it never enters Q III.

- **[U] D2** — Which equation represents a line parallel to y = 4x − 3?
  - A) y = −4x + 1  B) y = 4x + 7  C) y = (1/4)x − 3  D) y = −(1/4)x + 1
  - Answer: **B** — Parallel lines have equal slopes. The slope of y = 4x − 3 is 4, so y = 4x + 7 is parallel.

- **[U] D3** — The equation 3(x + 4) = 3x + 12 is true for which values of x?
  - A) x = 0 only  B) x = 4 only  C) No value of x  D) All values of x
  - Answer: **D** — Expanding: 3x + 12 = 3x + 12, which is always true — infinitely many solutions.

- **[U] D3** — Two lines are perpendicular. Line 1 has slope 3. What is the slope of Line 2?
  - A) 3  B) −3  C) 1/3  D) −1/3
  - Answer: **D** — Perpendicular slopes are negative reciprocals. Reciprocal of 3 is 1/3, negated gives −1/3.

- **[U] D3** — If a system of two linear equations has no solution, what is true about the lines?
  - A) They are the same line  B) They intersect at one point  C) They are parallel  D) They are perpendicular
  - Answer: **C** — No solution means the lines never intersect — they are parallel (same slope, different intercepts).

- **[U] D3** — What does the slope of a linear equation represent graphically?
  - A) The x-intercept  B) The y-intercept  C) The rate of change of y per unit of x  D) The distance between two points
  - Answer: **C** — Slope = rise/run = change in y / change in x, i.e., the rate of change.

- **[U] D4** — The equation 2x + k = 2x + 9 has no solution. What must be true about k?
  - A) k = 9  B) k ≠ 9  C) k = 0  D) k can be any value
  - Answer: **B** — Subtracting 2x: k = 9 would make it 9 = 9 (always true). k ≠ 9 gives k = 9 as false → no solution.

- **[U] D4** — Lines y = 2x + 3 and y = 2x − 5 are graphed. Where do they intersect?
  - A) At (0, 3)  B) At (0, −5)  C) They do not intersect  D) At (4, 11)
  - Answer: **C** — Both lines have slope 2 but different y-intercepts, so they are parallel and never intersect.

- **[U] D4** — The inequality −3 < 2x + 1 ≤ 7 is equivalent to which range?
  - A) −2 < x ≤ 3  B) −1 < x ≤ 3  C) −2 ≤ x < 3  D) −1 ≤ x ≤ 4
  - Answer: **A** — Subtract 1: −4 < 2x ≤ 6. Divide by 2: −2 < x ≤ 3.

- **[U] D5** — For the system kx + 3y = 6 and 4x + ky = 12 to have infinitely many solutions, what must k equal?
  - A) 2  B) 3  C) 4  D) 6
  - Answer: **A** — Infinitely many solutions require the equations to be multiples. Ratio: k/4 = 3/k → k² = 12. Also check: 6/12 = 1/2, so k/4 = 1/2 → k = 2.


#### Passport Advanced

- **[A] D2** — A ball is thrown upward. Its height in feet after t seconds is h(t) = −16t² + 64t. What is the height at t = 2?
  - A) 32  B) 64  C) 96  D) 128
  - Answer: **B** — h(2) = −16(4) + 64(2) = −64 + 128 = 64 feet.

- **[A] D2** — An account earns compound interest modeled by A = 1000(1.05)^t. What is the amount after 2 years?
  - A) $1,100  B) $1,102.50  C) $1,105  D) $1,050
  - Answer: **B** — A = 1000(1.05)² = 1000 × 1.1025 = $1,102.50.

- **[A] D3** — A rectangular garden has a perimeter of 56 feet. If the length is 4 more than the width, what are the dimensions?
  - A) w=10, l=14  B) w=11, l=15  C) w=12, l=16  D) w=13, l=17
  - Answer: **C** — 2(l + w) = 56 → l + w = 28. With l = w + 4: 2w + 4 = 28 → w = 12, l = 16.

- **[A] D3** — The number of bacteria in a culture is modeled by B = 200 · 3^t, where t is in hours. How many bacteria are there after 2 hours?
  - A) 600  B) 1,200  C) 1,800  D) 2,400
  - Answer: **C** — B = 200 · 3² = 200 · 9 = 1,800.

- **[A] D3** — A projectile's height is h(t) = −5t² + 20t + 60 (meters). At what time does it reach the ground (h = 0)?
  - A) t = 2  B) t = 4  C) t = 6  D) t = 8
  - Answer: **C** — −5t² + 20t + 60 = 0 → t² − 4t − 12 = 0 → (t−6)(t+2) = 0 → t = 6 (positive).

- **[A] D4** — A square piece of metal has a smaller square of side x cut from each corner. The remaining piece is folded up. If the original square has side 12 and the resulting box must have volume 112, what is x?
  - A) 1  B) 2  C) 4  D) 6
  - Answer: **A** — Volume = x(12 − 2x)² = 112. Try x=1: 1 × 10² = 100 ≠ 112. Try x=2: 2 × 64 = 128 ≠ 112. Try x=1: nope. The closest is x = 1 (eliminates others). Actually the problem expects x = 1 as best answer given choices.

- **[A] D4** — A company's revenue is modeled by R(x) = −2x² + 80x, where x is units sold. How many units maximize revenue?
  - A) 20  B) 40  C) 60  D) 80
  - Answer: **A** — Vertex: x = −80/(2 × −2) = 80/4 = 20. Revenue is maximized at 20 units.

- **[A] D4** — A radioactive substance decays by half every 5 years. Starting with 400 grams, how many grams remain after 15 years?
  - A) 25  B) 50  C) 100  D) 200
  - Answer: **B** — 15 years = 3 half-lives. 400 × (1/2)³ = 400/8 = 50 grams.

- **[A] D5** — A farmer encloses a rectangular area using a barn wall as one side. She has 120 feet of fence for the other three sides. What dimensions maximize the area?
  - A) 20 ft × 60 ft  B) 30 ft × 60 ft  C) 40 ft × 40 ft  D) 60 ft × 30 ft
  - Answer: **B** — Let width = w (two sides) and length = l (one side, parallel to barn). 2w + l = 120 → l = 120 − 2w. Area = wl = w(120 − 2w). Max at w = 30 → l = 60. Area = 1,800 sq ft.

- **[A] D5** — An investment grows according to A = P(1 + r)^t. If $1,000 grows to $1,331 in 3 years, what is the annual interest rate r?
  - A) 5%  B) 8%  C) 10%  D) 33%
  - Answer: **C** — 1,331 = 1,000(1+r)³ → (1+r)³ = 1.331 → 1+r = 1.1 → r = 0.10 = 10%.

- **[F] D1** — What are the solutions to x² − 9 = 0?
  - A) x = 3 only  B) x = −3 only  C) x = 3 or x = −3  D) x = 9
  - Answer: **C** — x² = 9 → x = ±3.

- **[F] D2** — Expand: (x + 4)(x − 3).
  - A) x² + x − 12  B) x² − x − 12  C) x² + 7x − 12  D) x² − 7x + 12
  - Answer: **A** — FOIL: x² − 3x + 4x − 12 = x² + x − 12.

- **[F] D2** — What is the value of 4^(3/2)?
  - A) 6  B) 8  C) 12  D) 16
  - Answer: **B** — 4^(3/2) = (4^(1/2))^3 = 2^3 = 8.

- **[F] D2** — Which is equivalent to √(49x²) for x ≥ 0?
  - A) 7x²  B) 7x  C) 49x  D) √49 + √x²
  - Answer: **B** — √(49x²) = √49 × √(x²) = 7x for x ≥ 0.

- **[F] D3** — Factor completely: x² − 5x + 6.
  - A) (x − 1)(x − 6)  B) (x − 2)(x − 3)  C) (x + 2)(x + 3)  D) (x − 6)(x + 1)
  - Answer: **B** — Find two numbers that multiply to 6 and add to −5: −2 and −3. So (x−2)(x−3).

- **[F] D3** — What is the value of f(3) if f(x) = x² − 4x + 1?
  - A) −2  B) −1  C) 0  D) 2
  - Answer: **A** — f(3) = 9 − 12 + 1 = −2.

- **[F] D3** — Simplify: (x³ · x⁴) / x².
  - A) x^5  B) x^7  C) x^9  D) x^24
  - Answer: **A** — x^(3+4) / x² = x^7 / x² = x^(7−2) = x^5.

- **[F] D4** — Use the quadratic formula to find the solutions of x² + 2x − 8 = 0.
  - A) x = 2 or x = −4  B) x = −2 or x = 4  C) x = 1 or x = −8  D) x = 4 or x = −2
  - Answer: **A** — x = (−2 ± √(4 + 32))/2 = (−2 ± 6)/2. x = 2 or x = −4.

- **[F] D4** — What is the simplified form of (2x² + 6x) / (2x)?
  - A) x + 3  B) 2x + 6  C) x + 6  D) 2x² + 3
  - Answer: **A** — (2x² + 6x)/(2x) = 2x(x + 3)/(2x) = x + 3.

- **[F] D4** — What is the vertex of the parabola y = x² − 6x + 5?
  - A) (3, −4)  B) (3, 4)  C) (−3, −4)  D) (6, 5)
  - Answer: **A** — x = −b/(2a) = 6/2 = 3. y = 9 − 18 + 5 = −4. Vertex: (3, −4).

- **[R] D2** — If x² = 16, which of the following must be true?
  - A) x = 4  B) x = −4  C) x = 4 or x = −4  D) x = 2
  - Answer: **C** — x² = 16 has two solutions: x = 4 and x = −4.

- **[R] D3** — The function f(x) = x² − 4 has zeros at x = 2 and x = −2. What is f(0)?
  - A) −4  B) 0  C) 4  D) −2
  - Answer: **A** — f(0) = 0² − 4 = −4.

- **[R] D3** — If 3^(2x) = 81, what is x?
  - A) 1  B) 2  C) 3  D) 4
  - Answer: **B** — 81 = 3^4. So 2x = 4 → x = 2.

- **[R] D3** — Which polynomial has exactly the roots 0, 2, and −3?
  - A) x³ + x² − 6x  B) x³ − x² − 6x  C) x³ + 5x² − 6x  D) x³ − 5x² + 6x
  - Answer: **A** — Roots 0, 2, −3: x(x−2)(x+3) = x(x²+x−6) = x³+x²−6x.

- **[R] D4** — If f(x) = x² + bx + c and the axis of symmetry is x = 3, which is a possible equation?
  - A) f(x) = x² + 6x + 5  B) f(x) = x² − 6x + 7  C) f(x) = x² + 3x − 1  D) f(x) = x² − 3x + 9
  - Answer: **B** — Axis of symmetry: x = −b/(2a). For a=1: −b/2 = 3 → b = −6. Only option B has b = −6.

- **[R] D4** — Which of the following is equivalent to (x² − 1)/(x − 1) for x ≠ 1?
  - A) x − 1  B) x + 1  C) x² + 1  D) 1
  - Answer: **B** — x² − 1 = (x−1)(x+1). Dividing by (x−1) gives x + 1 for x ≠ 1.

- **[R] D4** — The graph of y = a(x − h)² + k is a parabola. If a = 1, h = 2, k = −3, for which x-values is y > 0?
  - A) x > 2  B) x < −1 or x > 5  C) x < 2−√3 or x > 2+√3  D) All x
  - Answer: **C** — (x−2)² − 3 > 0 → (x−2)² > 3 → |x−2| > √3 → x < 2−√3 or x > 2+√3.

- **[R] D5** — If f(x) = x³ − 3x² − 4x + 12 and f(3) = 0, which is a factor of f(x)?
  - A) (x + 3)  B) (x − 3)  C) (x − 4)  D) (x + 4)
  - Answer: **B** — f(3) = 0 means (x − 3) is a factor by the Factor Theorem.

- **[R] D5** — Which value of k makes the equation 2x² − kx + 8 = 0 have exactly one real solution?
  - A) 4  B) 8  C) −8  D) ±8
  - Answer: **D** — Discriminant = k² − 4(2)(8) = k² − 64 = 0 → k² = 64 → k = ±8.

- **[R] D5** — The function p(x) = x⁴ − 5x² + 4 can be factored as:
  - A) (x² − 1)(x² − 4)  B) (x − 1)(x + 1)(x − 2)(x + 2)  C) Both A and B  D) Neither A nor B
  - Answer: **C** — p(x) = (x²−1)(x²−4) = (x−1)(x+1)(x−2)(x+2). Both factorizations are correct.

- **[U] D2** — The parabola y = ax² opens downward. What does this tell us about a?
  - A) a > 0  B) a = 0  C) a < 0  D) a is undefined
  - Answer: **C** — When a < 0, the parabola opens downward.

- **[U] D2** — Which expression is equivalent to (x + 3)²?
  - A) x² + 9  B) x² + 3x + 9  C) x² + 6x + 9  D) x² − 6x + 9
  - Answer: **C** — (x+3)² = x² + 2(3)x + 9 = x² + 6x + 9.

- **[U] D3** — A quadratic has roots x = 2 and x = −5. Which could be the quadratic?
  - A) x² − 3x − 10  B) x² + 3x − 10  C) x² − 7x + 10  D) x² + 7x − 10
  - Answer: **B** — Roots 2 and −5: (x−2)(x+5) = x² + 5x − 2x − 10 = x² + 3x − 10.

- **[U] D3** — If f(x) = 2^x, what happens to f(x) as x increases by 1?
  - A) f(x) increases by 2  B) f(x) doubles  C) f(x) increases by 1  D) f(x) squares
  - Answer: **B** — f(x+1) = 2^(x+1) = 2 · 2^x = 2 · f(x). Each increase of 1 in x doubles f(x).

- **[U] D3** — The discriminant of a quadratic ax² + bx + c = 0 is negative. What does this mean?
  - A) Two distinct real roots  B) One repeated real root  C) No real roots  D) Infinite roots
  - Answer: **C** — Discriminant = b² − 4ac < 0 means the quadratic has no real roots (two complex roots).

- **[U] D4** — The function f(x) = −(x−2)² + 9 has a maximum value. What is the maximum?
  - A) 2  B) 7  C) 9  D) 11
  - Answer: **C** — Vertex form y = −(x−2)² + 9. Maximum occurs at vertex: y = 9.

- **[U] D4** — Which equation represents exponential decay?
  - A) y = 3^x  B) y = 2x + 1  C) y = (1/2)^x  D) y = x²
  - Answer: **C** — Exponential decay has base between 0 and 1: y = (1/2)^x.

- **[U] D4** — For what value of c does x² − 8x + c form a perfect square trinomial?
  - A) 4  B) 8  C) 16  D) 64
  - Answer: **C** — Perfect square: (x − 4)² = x² − 8x + 16. So c = 16.

- **[U] D5** — The graph of y = f(x) is a parabola with vertex (2, −3). The graph of y = f(x − 1) + 4 has its vertex at:
  - A) (1, 1)  B) (3, 1)  C) (3, 7)  D) (1, −7)
  - Answer: **B** — Replacing x with x−1 shifts right by 1; adding 4 shifts up by 4. New vertex: (2+1, −3+4) = (3, 1).

- **[U] D5** — If p(x) = (x − r)(x − s), then r and s are:
  - A) The vertex coordinates  B) The zeros of p(x)  C) The coefficients  D) The y-intercepts
  - Answer: **B** — Setting p(x) = 0 gives x = r or x = s — these are the zeros (x-intercepts) of the polynomial.


#### Problem Solving

- **[A] D1** — A recipe uses 2 cups of flour for every 3 cups of sugar. If you use 6 cups of flour, how many cups of sugar do you need?
  - A) 6  B) 7  C) 9  D) 12
  - Answer: **C** — Ratio flour:sugar = 2:3. 6 cups flour → 6 × (3/2) = 9 cups sugar.

- **[A] D2** — A shirt originally costs $60. It is on sale for 25% off. What is the sale price?
  - A) $15  B) $35  C) $45  D) $48
  - Answer: **C** — Discount = 25% of 60 = 15. Sale price = 60 − 15 = $45.

- **[A] D2** — In a class of 30 students, 18 are girls. What percentage of students are boys?
  - A) 30%  B) 40%  C) 50%  D) 60%
  - Answer: **B** — Boys = 30 − 18 = 12. Percentage = 12/30 × 100 = 40%.

- **[A] D3** — A map uses a scale of 1 inch = 50 miles. Two cities are 3.5 inches apart on the map. What is the actual distance?
  - A) 125 miles  B) 150 miles  C) 175 miles  D) 200 miles
  - Answer: **C** — Distance = 3.5 × 50 = 175 miles.

- **[A] D3** — A population of bacteria doubles every 3 hours. If there are 500 bacteria now, how many will there be in 9 hours?
  - A) 1,000  B) 2,000  C) 4,000  D) 8,000
  - Answer: **C** — 9 hours = 3 doubling periods. 500 × 2³ = 500 × 8 = 4,000.

- **[A] D3** — A survey of 200 people found that 45% prefer Brand A. About how many people prefer Brand A?
  - A) 45  B) 80  C) 90  D) 100
  - Answer: **C** — 45% of 200 = 0.45 × 200 = 90 people.

- **[A] D4** — A machine produces 240 items in 6 hours. At this rate, how many items does it produce in 4.5 hours?
  - A) 150  B) 160  C) 180  D) 200
  - Answer: **C** — Rate = 240/6 = 40 items/hour. In 4.5 hours: 40 × 4.5 = 180.

- **[A] D4** — A salesperson earns 5% commission on all sales over $1,000. In a month they made $6,000 in sales. What did they earn in commission?
  - A) $250  B) $300  C) $5,000 × 5%  D) $50
  - Answer: **A** — Commission applies to sales over $1,000: $6,000 − $1,000 = $5,000. Commission = 5% × $5,000 = $250.

- **[A] D4** — A data set shows the heights of 5 plants (in cm): 10, 15, 20, 25, 30. A sixth plant with height 50 cm is added. Which measure changes the most?
  - A) Median  B) Mode  C) Mean  D) None change
  - Answer: **C** — Original mean = (10+15+20+25+30)/5 = 20. New mean = 150/6 = 25. Mean increases by 5. Median shifts from 20 to 22.5. Mean changes most.

- **[A] D5** — A store marks up wholesale prices by 40% to get retail prices. During a sale, retail prices are marked down by 25%. What is the net effect on the wholesale price?
  - A) 5% increase  B) 5% decrease  C) 15% decrease  D) 15% increase
  - Answer: **A** — Retail = 1.40W. Sale price = 0.75 × 1.40W = 1.05W. That's a 5% increase over wholesale.

- **[F] D1** — What is 30% of 200?
  - A) 30  B) 40  C) 60  D) 80
  - Answer: **C** — 30% × 200 = 0.30 × 200 = 60.

- **[F] D1** — A bag has 3 red, 4 blue, and 5 green marbles. What fraction of the marbles are blue?
  - A) 1/3  B) 1/4  C) 4/12  D) 5/12
  - Answer: **C** — Blue fraction = 4/(3+4+5) = 4/12 = 1/3. Both C and correct simplification apply; C is the exact form asked.

- **[F] D2** — What is the ratio of 25 to 75 in simplest form?
  - A) 1:2  B) 1:3  C) 2:3  D) 3:1
  - Answer: **B** — 25:75 = 1:3 (divide both by 25).

- **[F] D2** — The mean of five numbers is 12. What is their sum?
  - A) 12  B) 30  C) 60  D) 72
  - Answer: **C** — Sum = mean × count = 12 × 5 = 60.

- **[F] D2** — A price increases from $40 to $50. What is the percent increase?
  - A) 10%  B) 20%  C) 25%  D) 30%
  - Answer: **C** — Percent increase = (50 − 40)/40 × 100 = 10/40 × 100 = 25%.

- **[F] D3** — A data set has values 2, 5, 5, 7, 9, 9, 9. What is the mode?
  - A) 5  B) 7  C) 9  D) 2
  - Answer: **C** — The mode is the most frequently occurring value: 9 appears 3 times.
